A new YouGov survey <https://acasnational.cmail19.com/t/r-l-thkreuk-nukuduutrl-y/> , commissioned by Acas, asked employees to consider what would make them the most angry while at work._x000D_
_x000D_
Nearly half (49%) of employees said that people that are perceived not to be doing their job properly is the thing that makes them angriest at work._x000D_
_x000D_
Acas Head of Individual Dispute Resolution, Stewart Gee, said: "Unresolved emotions over things that seem unfair can have a detrimental effect at work and it is important for workplace conflict <https://acasnational.cmail19.com/t/r-l-thkreuk-nukuduutrl-j/>  to be addressed at the earliest possible opportunity._x000D_
_x000D_
"An informal resolution <https://acasnational.cmail19.com/t/r-l-thkreuk-nukuduutrl-t/>  through an initial chat or mediation can help organisations prevent the cost and stress of more formal procedures, such as an employment tribunal."_x000D_
_x000D_
 <https://i1.cmail19.com/ei/r/66/781/86D/201012/csfinal/stewart1-ce1c8914e9ce6eca.png> _x000D_
